  49. Been using a 7505 for years and years now. Ordered my annual-ish replacement blade, and it appears that Braun \\"upgraded\\" the design. The original blades were very thin (20% blade and 80% open space between blades.) In the new design it's more 50-50 of blade and open space. In practical terms, this means there is less space in the cutter opening for your beard to get into to be trimmed off. Where my wonderful shaver used to glide across my face, making it's pleasant buzzing noise, and leaving a nice clean smooth shave, with the new blade it now seems to be running slower (more blade mass to move), and it no longer glides but required more force to shave. Additionally, forget getting a smooth shave unless you have a lot of time, what used to take 2 or three passes now takes 10 or 15 to get near the same effect. I say near because, at least for me, it's not a smooth shave. I've stayed true to Braun for a very long time, but it appears it may be time to look at alternative brand electric shavers.

  51. The Braun company are constantly innovating, changing their razors and blades and even introducing the over-the-top \\"Clean & Charge\\" system that will scrub down your electric razor and keep it clean and sharp a lot longer. Unfortunately, not all innovations have been for the best, so if you own a Braun electric razor, you should probably check out my notes here and some of the comments that have followed this review.<br /><br />I've had my Braun 7000 series electric razor for a long time now, and I even have the \\"Clean & Charge\\" system that flushes the heads and charges the battery. I love the thing--it helps me not have to shave with a blade every day.<br /><br />The problem is, these things wear down so gradually it's hard to notice when it gets bad...until you replace it. I try to replace mine every year and a half, and every time I do I'm reminded how much better my Braun works when it's got a new blade and foil.<br /><br />This is my second Braun and I've had it for 7 years now. My first lasted me 16 years. Although the price can be steep, it's worth the effort to pick one up and remind yourself why you bought an electric razor in the first place.<br /><br />NOTE: These blades are for my 7000 series, but if you look over the compatibility details (and the alternate listings here at Amazon), you will see that the \\"30B\\" series are compatible with other razors, such as the 8585. This is important to know because Braun recently changed their blade and foil system for some series to the \\"51S\\"...and are getting customers complaining about having their face chewed off by the bigger-bladed 51S. If you're having problems with your Braun, check the listings here at Amazon to see if your razor is capable of using the 30S head: it has smaller blades, a finer foil design, and in my opinion provides a smoother shave than even the previous iteration of the 30B.

In the photos below, the 30b is on the left; the 51s is on the right. The 30b has a continuous squiggle in the central longer-hair channel of the foil and thicker cutter blades; the 51s has a gated central channel and thinner, more knife-like cutter blades. I believe that this is what lends a smoother, faster, more comfortable shave with the 30b than the 51s. Whatever the reason, buy the 30b and enjoy shaving again.<br /><br />One final note: $24.99 for one Braun 30b replacement pack is the list price, here.   277. Braun really messed up when they switched from the blade style cutter to the wide slot cutter. Not only does the wide blade cutter not cut as well as the thin blade cutter... pulling at hairs and taking longer... I have noticed it makes the shaver motor work much harder, leading to additional wear and less shave time per charge. The actual RPM the motor runs at is considerably lower with the wide blades. Here's how I &#34;proved&#34; this out. I used my 7526 shaver until the recharge light came on. Then I did about 1-2 more shaves, enough that the motor was starting to slow down. Then I manually cleaned the shaver head, just in case. I ran the shaver, just holding it in the air in front of me, as well as next to my ear. I swapped the old style vs new style cutter back to back using the same foil, and repeated. Just turn it on in the air and note the pitch of the hum of the motor. The wide blade cutter causes a noticeably lower pitch motor hum! That extra surface area between the foil and cutters means there is a LOT more friction for the motor to overcome. I've had this shaver about 13 years and I can't complain from the standpoint that I have gotten my money's worth. These German made Braun shavers are amazing compared to the later Chinese models. But this is such a fundamental design mistake that I am left shaking my head. How could the designers not see this? How could they think having all that metal rubbing against the foil wouldn't have a negative effect? Does not make me want to buy another Braun.

The one major complaint is that the original cutting system would grab and yank out facial hair which hurts. It seemed to be related to that tooth shaped cutter, but either way I was ready at this point to buy a Panasonic. It was mentioned that this assembly does not grab hairs.... that I can attest to as I shaved as I always did and it did not grab once. I have a goatee and I usually shave my fave first before trimming it. Definite improvement and of course the 30B cutter is about $15 less than the 51S which is nice as well.<br /><br />The reason for the 4-stars and not 5-stars is that I am still not 100% pleased with the way it cuts overall. I have used Norelco rotary razors and after switching to the Braun, I swore I would never go back as it was a huge improvement. The problem is that there ends up being particular hairs that it will not cut without going at a handful different attempts and angles. With that said, I still give the razor setup a thumbs up. Other than that it brought the razor back to life and no more pulled hairs.<br /><br />Also to dispel any myths--- it fits. I popped off my original parts and installed this without any issues. 5-seconds is all it takes to change the cutter and foil. The attachment post and everything were exactly the same and this part is made in Germany. And to reiterate, the only perceptible difference that you will see is the center saw tooth part and the color of the plastic--- otherwise it looks the same. If the rest of my razor is still functional in a year--- then I'll buy another one of the 30B's to bring it back to life otherwise, I may try a Panasonic to see how I like it.<br /><br />Feb 2016: Just bought my third one and now that I look back, I do need to replace it more often. The last one lasted 2-years and was still going, just not as sharp as it could be. Once again, the price was right and I am happy with the results.zor is still functional in a year--- then I'll buy another one of the 30B's to bring it back to life otherwise, I may try a Panasonic to see how I like it.   792. In my experience the foil design of the 30b is FAR superior to the foil design of the 51s. The larger hexagon shaped holes in the 51s seem to allow a little &#34;wiggle' in the hair shaft as the block is cutting it, thereby creating a tugging/pulling force on the hair rather than cleanly shearing it. For me, the foil pattern on the 30b does a MUCH better job holding/stabilizing the hair so the block/blade below can make a clean cut without any tugging/pulling. Of course, this problem becomes more and more noticeable with longer intervals between shaving and/or as the blade edges deteriorate over time. If you're a daily shaver and/or change the block/foil frequently there's probably no discernible difference between the two but for anyone who, like me, goes a couple days between shaving and/or likes to maximize the life of the blade then the 30b is superior.

  795. I was leery about ordering the 30b, when the one I should be ordering was a 51s. But after reading what others said about this one and how it works better, I thought that I would give it a try. It does cost less than the 51s and the reasons given for buying the 30b made since. But my biggest concern was would the 30b fit and work in my Aviator, well it does and it does give a very close shave again. The reason that I bought a new set was because the foil on my shaver had developed a hole in it. So I was trying to look around and find the best price for the correct product and I think that this is it.<br /><br />Another tip for those of you that have the Braun razors that have the alcohol cleaning system, you can save yourself some money by replacing the alcohol yourself. When you have a new container, put it on a level surface and mark the level of the alcohol in the container with a permanent marker, so that you know how much denatured alcohol to pour in when you go to refill it yourself. You need to use denatured alcohol when you refill the container, because the denatured alcohol has less water in it than rubbing alcohol, you can find denatured alcohol in the painting section of most stores. Do not wash out the old containers with water, just try to get out as much of the old alcohol as you can, you don't want any water in the container that you cannot get out. Add one half teaspoon of the lemon oil and one half teaspoon of sewing machine oil to the container and then pour in the denatured alcohol to the mark that you put on it when it was new. Do not over fill the container, the cleaning system has a level sensor in it and if it is overfilled you will have to pour out some of liquid until it will work. Also do not put too much lemon oil in you mixture it will help to take away the finish on the plastic parts. By doing this you can save yourself some money by not having to continually buy the new containers and still have a clean razor.
